fut = <Future cancelled>, timeout = 10.0

async def wait_for(fut, timeout, *, loop=None):
"""Wait for the single Future or coroutine to complete, with timeout.

Coroutine will be wrapped in Task.

Returns result of the Future or coroutine. When a timeout occurs,
it cancels the task and raises TimeoutError. To avoid the task
cancellation, wrap it in shield().

If the wait is cancelled, the task is also cancelled.

This function is a coroutine.
"""
if loop is None:
loop = events.get_event_loop()

if timeout is None:
return await fut

if timeout <= 0:
fut = ensure_future(fut, loop=loop)

if fut.done():
return fut.result()

fut.cancel()
raise futures.TimeoutError()

waiter = loop.create_future()
timeout_handle = loop.call_later(timeout, _release_waiter, waiter)
cb = functools.partial(_release_waiter, waiter)

fut = ensure_future(fut, loop=loop)
fut.add_done_callback(cb)

try:
# wait until the future completes or the timeout
try:
await waiter
except futures.CancelledError:
fut.remove_done_callback(cb)
fut.cancel()
raise

if fut.done():
return fut.result()
else:
fut.remove_done_callback(cb)
# We must ensure that the task is not running
# after wait_for() returns.
# See https://bugs.python.org/issue32751
await _cancel_and_wait(fut, loop=loop)
> raise futures.TimeoutError()

fut = <Future cancelled>, timeout = 10.0

async def wait_for(fut, timeout, *, loop=None):
"""Wait for the single Future or coroutine to complete, with timeout.

Coroutine will be wrapped in Task.

Returns result of the Future or coroutine. When a timeout occurs,
it cancels the task and raises TimeoutError. To avoid the task
cancellation, wrap it in shield().

If the wait is cancelled, the task is also cancelled.

This function is a coroutine.
"""
if loop is None:
loop = events.get_event_loop()

if timeout is None:
return await fut

if timeout <= 0:
fut = ensure_future(fut, loop=loop)

if fut.done():
return fut.result()

fut.cancel()
raise futures.TimeoutError()

waiter = loop.create_future()
timeout_handle = loop.call_later(timeout, _release_waiter, waiter)
cb = functools.partial(_release_waiter, waiter)

fut = ensure_future(fut, loop=loop)
fut.add_done_callback(cb)

try:
# wait until the future completes or the timeout
try:
await waiter
except futures.CancelledError:
fut.remove_done_callback(cb)
fut.cancel()
raise

if fut.done():
return fut.result()
else:
fut.remove_done_callback(cb)
# We must ensure that the task is not running
# after wait_for() returns.
# See https://bugs.python.org/issue32751
await _cancel_and_wait(fut, loop=loop)
> raise futures.TimeoutError()

fut = <Future cancelled>, timeout = 10.0

async def wait_for(fut, timeout, *, loop=None):
"""Wait for the single Future or coroutine to complete, with timeout.

Coroutine will be wrapped in Task.

Returns result of the Future or coroutine. When a timeout occurs,
it cancels the task and raises TimeoutError. To avoid the task
cancellation, wrap it in shield().

If the wait is cancelled, the task is also cancelled.

This function is a coroutine.
"""
if loop is None:
loop = events.get_event_loop()

if timeout is None:
return await fut

if timeout <= 0:
fut = ensure_future(fut, loop=loop)

if fut.done():
return fut.result()

fut.cancel()
raise futures.TimeoutError()

waiter = loop.create_future()
timeout_handle = loop.call_later(timeout, _release_waiter, waiter)
cb = functools.partial(_release_waiter, waiter)

fut = ensure_future(fut, loop=loop)
fut.add_done_callback(cb)

try:
# wait until the future completes or the timeout
try:
await waiter
except futures.CancelledError:
fut.remove_done_callback(cb)
fut.cancel()
raise

if fut.done():
return fut.result()
else:
fut.remove_done_callback(cb)
# We must ensure that the task is not running
# after wait_for() returns.
# See https://bugs.python.org/issue32751
await _cancel_and_wait(fut, loop=loop)
> raise futures.TimeoutError()

fut = <Future cancelled>, timeout = 10.0

async def wait_for(fut, timeout, *, loop=None):
"""Wait for the single Future or coroutine to complete, with timeout.

Coroutine will be wrapped in Task.

Returns result of the Future or coroutine. When a timeout occurs,
it cancels the task and raises TimeoutError. To avoid the task
cancellation, wrap it in shield().

If the wait is cancelled, the task is also cancelled.

This function is a coroutine.
"""
if loop is None:
loop = events.get_event_loop()

if timeout is None:
return await fut

if timeout <= 0:
fut = ensure_future(fut, loop=loop)

if fut.done():
return fut.result()

fut.cancel()
raise futures.TimeoutError()

waiter = loop.create_future()
timeout_handle = loop.call_later(timeout, _release_waiter, waiter)
cb = functools.partial(_release_waiter, waiter)

fut = ensure_future(fut, loop=loop)
fut.add_done_callback(cb)

try:
# wait until the future completes or the timeout
try:
await waiter
except futures.CancelledError:
fut.remove_done_callback(cb)
fut.cancel()
raise

if fut.done():
return fut.result()
else:
fut.remove_done_callback(cb)
# We must ensure that the task is not running
# after wait_for() returns.
# See https://bugs.python.org/issue32751
await _cancel_and_wait(fut, loop=loop)
> raise futures.TimeoutError()

headers: Dict[str, Any] = None,
) -> Msg:

assert self._resp_sub_prefix

)

headers: Dict[str, Any] = None,
) -> Msg:

using a single wildcard subscription that handles
the responses.

)

)

def execute_rdac_command(args):

site = None, use_vault = True, helpers = <class 'conftest.Helpers'>
format = 'csv'

@pytest.mark.parametrize("format", ["csv", "parquet"])
def test_dataset_save(site, use_vault, helpers, format):
"""Test case to save dataset and retrieve"""
name = f"test_dataset_save_{format}"
df = helpers.run_pipeline(site, use_vault, pipeline_text=f"""@dm:empty
--> @dm:addrow column1 = "Value00" & column2 = "Value01"
--> @dm:addrow column1 = "Value10" & column2 = "Value11"
--> @dm:save name="{name}" & format="{format}"
""")
assert df.shape[0] == 2, f"addrow should return 2 rows. But it returned {df.shape[0]} rows"
assert df.to_dict("records") == [{"column1": "Value00", "column2": "Value01"}, {"column1": "Value10", "column2": "Value11"}]

# Retrieve the dataset using savedlist and verify
df = helpers.run_pipeline(site, use_vault, pipeline_text="*dm:savedlist")
dataset = next((x for x in df.to_dict("records") if x["name"] == name), None)
assert dataset, f"Dataset {name} successfully added. But unable to retrieve it *dm:savedlist"
saved_time_str = dataset["saved_time"]
utc_timestr = saved_time_str + "+00:00"
assert (datetime.fromisoformat(utc_timestr).replace(tzinfo=None) - datetime.utcnow().replace(tzinfo=None)) < timedelta(seconds=30)

# Retrieve the dataset using recall and verify
df = helpers.run_pipeline(site, use_vault, pipeline_text=f"""@dm:recall name="{name}" """)
assert df.shape[0] == 2, f"addrow should return 2 rows. But it returned {df.shape[0]} rows"
assert df.to_dict("records") == [{"column1": "Value00", "column2": "Value01"}, {"column1": "Value10", "column2": "Value11"}]
> delete_dataset(name, helpers)

async def _request_new_style(
self,
subject: str,
payload: bytes,
timeout: float = 1,
headers: Dict[str, Any] = None,
) -> Msg:
if self.is_draining_pubs:
raise errors.ConnectionDrainingError

await self._init_request_sub()
assert self._resp_sub_prefix

token = self._nuid.next()
inbox = self._resp_sub_prefix[:]
inbox.extend(token)
future: asyncio.Future = asyncio.Future()
self._resp_map[token.decode()] = future
await self.publish(
subject, payload, reply=inbox.decode(), headers=headers
)

fut = <Future cancelled>, timeout = 10.0

async def wait_for(fut, timeout, *, loop=None):
"""Wait for the single Future or coroutine to complete, with timeout.

Coroutine will be wrapped in Task.

Returns result of the Future or coroutine. When a timeout occurs,
it cancels the task and raises TimeoutError. To avoid the task
cancellation, wrap it in shield().

If the wait is cancelled, the task is also cancelled.

This function is a coroutine.
"""
if loop is None:
loop = events.get_event_loop()

if timeout is None:
return await fut

if timeout <= 0:
fut = ensure_future(fut, loop=loop)

if fut.done():
return fut.result()

fut.cancel()
raise futures.TimeoutError()

waiter = loop.create_future()
timeout_handle = loop.call_later(timeout, _release_waiter, waiter)
cb = functools.partial(_release_waiter, waiter)

fut = ensure_future(fut, loop=loop)
fut.add_done_callback(cb)

try:
# wait until the future completes or the timeout
try:
await waiter
except futures.CancelledError:
fut.remove_done_callback(cb)
fut.cancel()
raise

if fut.done():
return fut.result()
else:
fut.remove_done_callback(cb)
# We must ensure that the task is not running
# after wait_for() returns.
# See https://bugs.python.org/issue32751
await _cancel_and_wait(fut, loop=loop)
> raise futures.TimeoutError()
E concurrent.futures._base.TimeoutError

self = <nats client v2.0.0>

timeout = 10.0, headers = None

async def _request_new_style(
self,
subject: str,
payload: bytes,
timeout: float = 1,
headers: Dict[str, Any] = None,
) -> Msg:
if self.is_draining_pubs:
raise errors.ConnectionDrainingError

if not self._resp_sub_prefix:
await self._init_request_sub()
assert self._resp_sub_prefix

# Use a new NUID for the token inbox and then use the future.
token = self._nuid.next()
inbox = self._resp_sub_prefix[:]
inbox.extend(token)
future: asyncio.Future = asyncio.Future()
self._resp_map[token.decode()] = future
await self.publish(
subject, payload, reply=inbox.decode(), headers=headers
)

# Wait for the response or give up on timeout.
try:
msg = await asyncio.wait_for(future, timeout)
return msg
except asyncio.TimeoutError:
# Double check that the token is there already.
self._resp_map.pop(token.decode())
future.cancel()
> raise errors.TimeoutError

async def _request_new_style(
self,
subject: str,
payload: bytes,
timeout: float = 1,
headers: Dict[str, Any] = None,
) -> Msg:
if self.is_draining_pubs:
raise errors.ConnectionDrainingError

if not self._resp_sub_prefix:
await self._init_request_sub()
assert self._resp_sub_prefix

# Use a new NUID for the token inbox and then use the future.
token = self._nuid.next()
inbox = self._resp_sub_prefix[:]
inbox.extend(token)
future: asyncio.Future = asyncio.Future()

async def wait_for(fut, timeout, *, loop=None):
"""Wait for the single Future or coroutine to complete, with timeout.

Coroutine will be wrapped in Task.

Returns result of the Future or coroutine. When a timeout occurs,
it cancels the task and raises TimeoutError. To avoid the task
cancellation, wrap it in shield().

If the wait is cancelled, the task is also cancelled.

This function is a coroutine.
"""
if loop is None:
loop = events.get_event_loop()

if timeout is None:
return await fut

if timeout <= 0:
fut = ensure_future(fut, loop=loop)

if fut.done():
return fut.result()

fut.cancel()
raise futures.TimeoutError()

waiter = loop.create_future()
timeout_handle = loop.call_later(timeout, _release_waiter, waiter)
cb = functools.partial(_release_waiter, waiter)

fut = ensure_future(fut, loop=loop)
fut.add_done_callback(cb)

try:
# wait until the future completes or the timeout
try:
await waiter
except futures.CancelledError:
fut.remove_done_callback(cb)
fut.cancel()
raise

if fut.done():
return fut.result()
else:
fut.remove_done_callback(cb)
# We must ensure that the task is not running
# after wait_for() returns.
# See https://bugs.python.org/issue32751
await _cancel_and_wait(fut, loop=loop)
> raise futures.TimeoutError()

async def _request_new_style(
self,
subject: str,
payload: bytes,
timeout: float = 1,
headers: Dict[str, Any] = None,
) -> Msg:
if self.is_draining_pubs:
raise errors.ConnectionDrainingError

if not self._resp_sub_prefix:
await self._init_request_sub()
assert self._resp_sub_prefix

# Use a new NUID for the token inbox and then use the future.
token = self._nuid.next()
inbox = self._resp_sub_prefix[:]
inbox.extend(token)
future: asyncio.Future = asyncio.Future()
self._resp_map[token.decode()] = future
await self.publish(
subject, payload, reply=inbox.decode(), headers=headers
)

# Wait for the response or give up on timeout.
try:
msg = await asyncio.wait_for(future, timeout)
return msg
except asyncio.TimeoutError:
# Double check that the token is there already.
self._resp_map.pop(token.decode())
future.cancel()

if timeout is None:
return await fut

if timeout <= 0:
fut = ensure_future(fut, loop=loop)

if fut.done():
return fut.result()

fut.cancel()
raise futures.TimeoutError()

waiter = loop.create_future()
timeout_handle = loop.call_later(timeout, _release_waiter, waiter)
cb = functools.partial(_release_waiter, waiter)

fut = ensure_future(fut, loop=loop)
fut.add_done_callback(cb)

try:
# wait until the future completes or the timeout
try:
await waiter
except futures.CancelledError:
fut.remove_done_callback(cb)
fut.cancel()
raise

if fut.done():
return fut.result()
else:
fut.remove_done_callback(cb)
# We must ensure that the task is not running
# after wait_for() returns.
# See https://bugs.python.org/issue32751
await _cancel_and_wait(fut, loop=loop)

async def _request_new_style(
self,
subject: str,
payload: bytes,
timeout: float = 1,
headers: Dict[str, Any] = None,
) -> Msg:
if self.is_draining_pubs:
raise errors.ConnectionDrainingError

if not self._resp_sub_prefix:
await self._init_request_sub()
assert self._resp_sub_prefix

# Use a new NUID for the token inbox and then use the future.
token = self._nuid.next()
inbox = self._resp_sub_prefix[:]
inbox.extend(token)
future: asyncio.Future = asyncio.Future()
self._resp_map[token.decode()] = future
await self.publish(
subject, payload, reply=inbox.decode(), headers=headers
)

# Wait for the response or give up on timeout.
try:
msg = await asyncio.wait_for(future, timeout)
return msg
except asyncio.TimeoutError:
# Double check that the token is there already.
self._resp_map.pop(token.decode())
future.cancel()
